# WordPress Ecommerce: WooCommerce

> Learn how to build an online store using one of the most popular and trusted ecommerce solutions for WordPress. WooCommerce provides advanced store management for physical, digital, and even subscription-based products in a clean and easy-to-understand package. Simply put, WordPress plus WooCommerce equals your online shopping portal on your terms. Join WooCommerce expert Patrick Rauland as he sho

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4) | 2h 39m | Beginner | 6K learners

- [[Patrick Rauland]]

#### What to know ahead of time
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] For this course, we'll be setting up WooCommerce on a WordPress website.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=4)** You don't need to know how to write WordPress code, but it would be helpful to have some WordPress knowledge, such as how to install WordPress itself, how to install themes and plugins, and how to add pages and posts.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=17)** If you'd like a refresher, I recommend WordPress Essential Training in the library.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=21)** I'll cover everything you need to know with WooCommerce, but knowing a bit about Ecommerce in general, such as the cost of acquisition, customer lifetime value, as well as how you plan to get people to your site, can be really helpful.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=33)** Basically, it'll be helpful if you know what you're going to sell and how you're going to sell it.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=37)** That'll make sure you set up your WooCommerce store correctly.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=40)** My WordPress Ecommerce course in the library covers all these fundamentals if you want to take that first.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=46)** Throughout this course we'll be using the free WooCommerce plugin.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=49)** The majority of the videos in this course will cover all of those free features, but some plugins will highlight premium plugins that do have a yearly fee.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/what-to-know-ahead-of-time?u=76281980&t=57)** You don't have to buy any of these premium plugins, as the course is designed around the free plugin, but we do show them to you so you know when and where they're useful.

### 1. Getting Started

#### Why WooCommerce?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you're a store owner or if you're a developer going to build a site for a client, you will either get asked to use WooCommerce or you will have to think about why you want to use WooCommerce.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=11)** WooCommerce has a couple of amazing things going for it.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=14)** First of all, it is built on WordPress.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=17)** That means that you can leverage all of the tools and services built on top of WordPress.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=22)** There are thousands of free plugins and themes available to you.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=26)** WordPress was created in 2003.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=29)** Normally, software doesn't make it into the teenage years because it unravels as people lose interest.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=34)** But this hasn't happened with WordPress.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=36)** It's only getting bigger and bigger, and the space is maturing.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=40)** No matter what you need, someone else has also had that need and developed a theme, plugin, or custom code to solve that issue.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=47)** The second selling point is that WooCommerce, like WordPress, is open source and GPL-licensed.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=53)** Open source means that you can look at every single line of code to see what it's doing.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=58)** You can rip out or edit any line of code that you want.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=61)** You could completely rewrite WooCommerce for your own purpose.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=64)** Because it's open source, you can literally do anything with it.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=67)** Most e-commerce platforms are hosted, and the source code is hidden, so there are things you won't be able to do.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=73)** The GPL license is a bit harder to explain.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=77)** The easiest way to understand it is that it's one of the most liberal licenses.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=81)** It lets you use the software however you want, for as long as you want, without having to pay.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=86)** What's great about the GPL from a business perspective is that even if the unthinkable happened and Automattic, the company behind WooCommerce, went out of business, the community could continue to develop WooCommerce and distribute it.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=98)** The third selling point is that WordPress is very strongly tied to content.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=103)** WordPress started out as a blogging platform, so there are thousands of plugins just about blogging, content, and SEO.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=110)** Many e-commerce platforms throw a blog on as an afterthought.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=114)** It isn't a primary feature, and it's pretty basic.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=117)** If you plan on doing content marketing for your store, then having a fully featured blog is essential, and you should choose a platform that's tied strongly to content, like WordPress.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=127)** The fourth selling point is the huge number of developers that you have access to.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=131)** If you ever need something totally custom, there are hundreds of thousands of WordPress developers that you can reach out to.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=137)** On [Freelancer.com](https://Freelancer.com), they list 100,000 WordPress developers, and that's just one site.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=143)** Chances are there's a WordPress meetup in your town where you could meet a developer face to face.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=148)** So far, we've really only talked about WooCommerce and WordPress as platforms.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=152)** We haven't even gone into any of the features, and WooCommerce has a ton of features.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=158)** WooCommerce lets you sell physical products, downloadable goods, subscriptions, memberships, preorders, name-your-own-price products, and more.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=167)** It's incredibly customizable.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=169)** You can sell any type of product in any way you want.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=172)** It also integrates with some of the biggest payment gateways out there, so you can get paid however you want to get paid, whether that be through Stripe, PayPal, or any of the 100-plus official payment gateways on [WooCommerce.com](https://WooCommerce.com).
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=185)** It also integrates with all of the major shipping providers.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=187)** You can get live quotes from UPS, USPS, and FedEx.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=192)** You can export these orders into fulfillment software, like ShipStation and Ordoro.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=196)** And of course, you can print labels at home.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=199)** WooCommerce is a solid platform for store owners because it has a lot of integrations.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=203)** And it's solid for developers because of the open-source nature of the platform and how customizable it is.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/why-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=209)** Whether you're starting a new e-commerce store or replatforming from an older system, you can't go wrong with WooCommerce.

#### Setting up WordPress for eCommerce
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=0)** - We're going to create our own store with a pretty much, bare-bones WordPress web site.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=5)** You can follow along with your own WordPress site.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=8)** We'll be using the 2019 theme at first.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=11)** And later in the course, we're going to look into another great WooCommerce theme called Storefront.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=16)** You should be able to follow along with 2019 Storefront, or any other WordPress or WooCommerce theme that you have installed on your site.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=23)** There's a few pages that we should set up before we install WooCommerce.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=27)** I've already created and filled out an About page.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=31)** The About page is you telling your story to the customer.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=34)** I've also created a Contact page, which is where people can reach us.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=38)** If you need a refresher on creating pages, or installing themes, all of that is covered in the WordPress Essential Training course.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=45)** There's one thing that I want to show you here, that is a bit of a trick.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=48)** If you notice, I'll go back to the about page here, for some themes, comments might be enabled on your pages.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=56)** Comments make a lot of sense on blog posts, but not a lot of sense on pages.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=60)** So let's turn these off.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=62)** I'll go to the Admin, I'll go to Pages, and I'll select all of my pages here, go to Bulk Actions, change this to Edit, Apply, and Comments, Do not allow.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=76)** And then click Update.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=79)** I'll go back to my About page, scroll down, and I no longer see the comments box.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=87)** So that'll make our pages a little bit more page-like.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=90)** We should also set up Permalinks.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=92)** If you see the ?page_id=8, then you haven't set up Permalinks yet.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=98)** Let's go back to our Admin, and then go to Settings, Permalinks, and change this to any option other than Plain.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=106)** So, Day and name will work, Month and name will work, Numeric, Post name.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=110)** I'm a big fan of Day and name.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=113)** And click Save Changes.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=116)** We'll go back to our About page and refresh it, and now we have a much prettier Permalink.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=123)** This will work for our About page and Contact page, as well as our Product pages, which we'll create a little bit later.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-wordpress-for-ecommerce?u=76281980&t=129)** Now that our site is ready for eCommerce, let's move on to installing that WooCommerce plug-in.

### 2. Setting Up Shop with WooCommerce

#### Downloading and installing WooCommerce
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's get started by downloading and installing the WooCommerce plugin.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=4)** There's a couple of ways to do this.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=6)** The easiest way is to install the plugin from within your WordPress site.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=11)** Let's go to Plugins, Add New, then we can type in WooCommerce and install the one from Automatic, and that's it.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=23)** In a future video, we'll activate the plugin and cover the Welcome Wizard, and if you want to, you can skip ahead and do that right now.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=31)** The other way to install WooCommerce is to go through the official signup on [WooCommerce.com](https://WooCommerce.com).
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=36)** This way is going to be a bit longer, but they'll ask you a bunch of questions, and when we answer them, they'll know a little bit more about us.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=44)** That means, they'll be able to send us relevant content.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=47)** And if you're new to eCommerce, or WooCommerce, it's helpful to be on their newsletter and get content that's perfectly suited to you.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=54)** So, from the Home page on WooCommerce, there should be a button or a link called Get Started, which'll take us to [woocommerce.com/start](https://woocommerce.com/start).
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=63)** That will prompt us to create a [WordPress.com](https://WordPress.com) account.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=67)** Since Automatic is the company behind [WordPress.com](https://WordPress.com) and WooCommerce, they now share accounts so you only need one.

> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/downloading-and-installing-woocommerce?u=76281980&t=86)** If you have two-factor authentication enabled on your account, which, by the way, I always recommend, then you'll have to authenticate before continuing.

#### Installing Jetpack via the welcome wizard
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We're going to continue where we left off with the Welcome Wizard.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=4)** We filled out the shipping information, and we're going to click the button to continue to the recommended section.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=9)** This page prompts us to install a bunch of related services including the Storefront Theme, Automated Taxes, Mailchimp for Woo Commerce, and Facebook for Woo Commerce.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=20)** I highly recommend Storefront since it includes so much free functionality.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=24)** It is a great starting point for many stores.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=27)** If you've never built a Woo Commerce site before, give Storefront a try to see how everything looks in it, and then if you want to use a different theme later on, you can.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=35)** There is also a feature called Automated Taxes, which we definitely want to turn on.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=39)** This lets Woo Commerce services import tax rates for us.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=43)** Taxes are a really complex subject, The one limitation of Automated Taxes is that at the moment it only works when you have nexus in one region.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=55)** So if you have stores, employees, or warehouses in multiple states you'll very likely have nexus in those other states and you can't use this feature.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=69)** and later in this course I'll show you how you can configure your taxes manually.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=73)** The last two options are Mailchimp and Facebook.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=76)** We'll cover both of these a little bit later in this course.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=79)** So I'll actually deactivate them for right now.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=81)** Since we want Automated Taxes, we need to connect to [wordpress.com](https://wordpress.com), which powers all of this functionality.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=88)** And in order to do that we need to connect our store via Jetpack, which is a free plugin offered by [wordpress.com](https://wordpress.com).
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=95)** If you don't want to use Jetpack you don't have to.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=98)** You just won't be able to use the free live rates or the Automated Taxes included with it.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=105)** Let's click the button.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=107)** And while we're waiting for this to load, it's worth pointing out that you have to have a live site to use this functionality.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=113)** By live site, I mean something that is publicly accessible.

> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=117)** So, if you are developing the site locally, for example, then you can't connect to [wordpress.com](https://wordpress.com) and this functionality won't work.

> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-jetpack-via-the-welcome-wizard?u=76281980&t=124)** When you're developing an eCommerce site, there's a lot of functionality that needs to run on a publicly accessible site.

#### Adding an image to a product
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Earlier, we added the absolute bare bones for a project, which are the title and the price.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=6)** Next up are the most visual elements and that is the product photo.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=10)** The photo is one of the most important parts of your product page.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=14)** However, the data around what types of product images are still up in the air.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=19)** With certain industries, you want to have a large image.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=22)** And with some, you want to have an image with a bit of white space around it.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=25)** If we look at this research by conversion XL, we can see that for functional products, like cameras, hard drives, computers, et cetera, a large image tends to work better.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=36)** For design-heavy products, like fashion, jewelry, illustrations et cetera, an image with a bit of white space tends to work a little bit better.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=44)** The theory behind this is you need the white space to help viewers really appreciate the design.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=49)** Whereas for functional products, like hard drives, just show me the big image.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=52)** I don't need any white space to appreciate it.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=55)** So for H plus sports, we're selling protein bars, mineral water and supplements, which are more functional.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=60)** So we're going to want to use images that don't have too much white space.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=64)** I have an image on my desktop ready to go.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=67)** Before I upload it, I'm going to do one thing.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=69)** I'm going to make sure that my files names are more helpful for search engine optimization.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=74)** In WordPress, it's really hard to rename files once they've been uploaded.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=79)** So I always spend a few minutes doing this before I upload an image to my site.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=83)** So here's the image I want to use.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=86)** I'm going to click return, so I can edit it.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=88)** And I'm going to remove this 600 PX, Google doesn't need to know that.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=93)** And if you don't already have this, go ahead and put dashes between the words.

> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-an-image-to-a-product?u=76281980&t=98)** WordPress should automatically do that but I just like to make sure it's done right.

#### Adding categories and tags
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] You may have noticed that our product is uncategorized, or you may not see any category on the front end.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=7)** One of the things that we can do to make our products more discoverable is to add categories and tags to help our user browse to the right product.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=21)** For a store with a dozen or so products, you probably don't have to add categories and tags, but they're still useful, so I like to add them.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=29)** If you have twenty or more products, I definitely recommend adding categories and tags.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=34)** They really help people browse to the right product.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=37)** Let's add a category for this product.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=39)** We'll scroll down past our image and gallery, and we can see it's in the default category, Uncategorized.

> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=53)** And, if we wanted, we could add it to an existing category as a child category.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=60)** And once our category appears here, we can uncheck Uncategorized, click Update, and now let's take a look at the front end.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=73)** So we can see it's changed up here, Supplements, and this will take us to a product category page called "Supplements," and it's changed down here as well.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=85)** If you have a lot of categories, you can go to Products, Categories and bulk edit these.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=91)** We've talked a lot about categories, but we haven't yet talked about tags.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=95)** I tend to think of each product belonging to one category, but it could belong to any number of tags.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=102)** For example, I could have a mineral water category and then a blueberry tag, and anything that has blueberry flavoring could share that tag, so users who like that flavor can navigate between categories.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=115)** Tags are useful, but not nearly as useful as categories, so I won't be adding them to this site.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=120)** But if you have hundreds of products, it can be very useful for your users.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=125)** The one thing I want to caution you against is using the same words or phrases for both categories and tags.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=132)** So if I have a category called "Supplements," I shouldn't also have a tag called "Supplements."
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=138)** Choose one or the other.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=140)** This helps the user, and it helps search engines.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=142)** So even though it's tempting to think it's another way for your users to navigate, it's actually a bad practice and can confuse your users and search engines.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-categories-and-tags?u=76281980&t=150)** So if you have more than a dozen or so products, I recommend adding a category to each one.

> **Best Practices:** bad practice (1)

>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-digital-products?u=76281980&t=81)** But in most cases, your product will be both virtual and downloadable.

#### Adding descriptions
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the useful features about WooCommerce that is a bit hard to find is the short description.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=5)** That's a one or two-sentence description of your product that can be seen above the fold.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=9)** And what's great about it is you don't really need to scroll down to read it, and it's not buried in a tab.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=15)** If you have a short description set, it should be seen right here.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=19)** Let's go to the Admin to add this in.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=21)** I'll click on Edit Product.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=24)** Here's what's known as the full description which appears beneath the product and in a tab.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=31)** And here is the short description.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=34)** Let's go ahead and add one.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=37)** Let's click Update.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=40)** And let's see what this looks like on the front end.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=44)** There we go.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=46)** Five new easy-to-cook recipes that'll make you feel good about your food and your body.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=50)** This short description is what will convince users to read a little bit more, so right down here is where we'd see the full product description.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=59)** A lot of people forget to add the short description, or they add it last minute themselves.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/adding-descriptions?u=76281980&t=63)** Take a few minutes to craft a really good short description for each product, since it might be the one thing to convince the user to read more or click through your photos.

#### Importing products
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Patrick] If you don't have any of your own products, it can be tricky to follow the rest of this course and it's hard to imagine what your store could look like.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=8)** Luckily the WooCommerce team has already thought of this.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=11)** They've included dummy data that you can use.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=14)** There's two places where you can get this data.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=17)** One of them is built in to WooCommerce itself and it takes a few steps to set up.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=21)** The other is built into Storefront and it's very easy to set up.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=25)** In fact, it's just pressing a button.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=27)** If you're planning on using Storefront, you can skip ahead and install Storefront, and when you do, make sure you check the option to install dummy products.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=35)** It is by far the easiest way to import products.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=39)** Otherwise, you can use your own products, or, I'll show you how to use the dummy products built in to WooCommerce itself.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=45)** This is definitely a bit more work, but I want to show you a method that'll work for anyone no matter what theme you're using.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=52)** To import this data, we need to start in the Admin, then we'll go to Tools, and Import.

> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/importing-products?u=76281980&t=59)** Scroll down to WooCommerce products CSV, and click Run Importer.

#### Customizing the welcome page
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-welcome-page?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-welcome-page?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Every store has the Shop page, which is a page automatically created by WooCommerce.

#### Customizing the shop page
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The Shop page shows us all the products and categories in our store, and it's a default page created by WooCommerce.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=8)** And you can get to it through a number of ways, including the bread crumbs, the Cart page, and other pages.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=13)** So we want to make sure this page looks just as good as the home page.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=17)** Let's go to the Customizer, and in the Customizer, we can go to WooCommerce and then Product Catalog.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=25)** In here, we can change the defaults for the Shop page.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=28)** So we can choose between shoving products and showing categories.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=33)** There's our uncategorized category.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=37)** We can show both.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=40)** And if we scroll down, we can also change how many products per row we want to show, and how many rows per page.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=50)** If you aren't using Storefront, and you don't have these options, there's a useful plugin called the WooCommerce Product Archive Customizer, which helps you do similar things.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=59)** The options might not be in the same place, but you should be able to do something similar by following the documentation here.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=65)** One last thing before we move on.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=67)** Earlier, we customized the button colors, and colors don't really affect mobile devices differently than desktops.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=73)** But now that we're changing the layout, you should always be checking what your site looks like on tablet and on mobile.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=79)** So as you're changing rows and columns, make sure that your theme responds appropriately.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=85)** The Shop page, your front page, and the Product page are especially important.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=88)** Make sure the people are seeing something useful on all devices.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=92)** With Storefront, this shouldn't be an issue.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/customizing-the-shop-page?u=76281980&t=94)** But just check and be aware of what it looks like to someone who's on their phone.

### 5. Setting Up Shipping Options

#### Choosing shipping options
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Choosing a shipping provider and figuring out how you pay for that cost isn't an easy decision.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=5)** Some customers care about speed and want to have options and be able to choose the fastest option.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=11)** Many consumers want to have the cheapest option, including a free option, and concealing the cost of shipping in your profit margins may be the best bet.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=20)** Some customers want to have options because they have a preference.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=23)** I live in a building that USPS and FedEx can figure out, but UPS drops packages off at the office and doesn't leave a note.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=30)** This drives me bonkers, and if I have a choice for my building, I will always pick USPS or FedEx over UPS.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=37)** Of course, as a business, you want to make sure that you can pay for these shipping costs.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=41)** Sometimes that means charging the users the whole cost, some of the cost, or none of the cost, and generally speaking, you don't want to have dozens of shipping partners.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=50)** That means maintaining more business relationships and things are easier to get lost that way.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=55)** Many e-commerce companies will use one or two primary shipping partners.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=59)** If you have heavy or bulky items, you might need to use a third-party logistics company, or 3PL, to create a special shipping quote for you, and you need to estimate that in your e-commerce setup.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=70)** We're going to go over the most popular shipping options in WooCommerce, going from easiest to the most complex.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=76)** Ultimately, the decision on how you ship your products depends on your business and your customers.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=81)** I'm going to give you all of the options and I recommend picking one option to start.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/choosing-shipping-options?u=76281980&t=85)** Or, if you want, you can pick free shipping in addition to one other option to keep it simple.

#### Creating shipping zones
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=0)** - We're going to use a couple different ways to ship products.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=3)** But, to do so effectively, we need to specify a couple different regions.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=7)** We can use those regions as a cue, so that WooCommerce knows which shipping methods to use in which regions.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=13)** In WooCommerce, this functionality is called Shipping Zones, and zones can be as big as a country, and as small as a city or zip code.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=21)** A common way to use shipping zones it offer free pick-up, in addition to other options if you're in the same state or city, and you could have a shipping fee for the rest of the U.S., and then a different shipping fee worldwide.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=34)** Let's go to the admin and create these shipping zones.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=37)** Let's start by going to WooCommerce, Settings, and then Shipping.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=44)** Here we can see our existing zones.

> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=46)** We can see one for the country.

>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=58)** I'm going to call mine Local.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=60)** And, for a region, I could start with something like Colorado, where my store is located.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=65)** But, that's actually a little bit big, so I'm going to use something more sophisticated.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=69)** I'm going to limit this to specific zip codes.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=72)** I could type in 80201, 80202, etc.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=79)** Or, WooCommerce let's you use ranges.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=82)** So, I could type in 80201, ... 80202, or, all the way up to 80209.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=90)** Or, we can use wildcards.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=92)** So, 8020, anything.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=95)** This will let me display special shipping methods to people who are in my local area in Colorado, and who are limited to these specific zip codes near Denver.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=105)** Let's save changes.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=106)** And then, we can add shipping methods here.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=109)** Let's go back to our shipping zones.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=112)** Here we can see local, the United States, and everything else.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=116)** There's one more thing to be aware of.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=118)** You can prioritize zones.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=120)** You'll want to make sure you go from the most specific at the top, to the least specific at the bottom.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=125)** If you do it the other way around and have U.S. above local, then local will never get displayed to the customer.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=130)** WooCommerce will always use the first zone that matches the criteria, starting from the top.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=135)** So, let's click and drag local above the United States, and now all we have to do is add shipping methods to these zones.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/creating-shipping-zones?u=76281980&t=145)** Before customers can check out from this new zone, we will have to add shipping methods, which we'll cover in future videos.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (9), else. (2)

#### Setting up free shipping
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the things that consumers love more than a fair price is something that's free.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=4)** Free shipping is a great way to attract new customers.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=8)** There's some research from Forrester which highlights how much consumers value free shipping.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=12)** Specifically, 39% of them are willing to purchase additional products to earn free shipping.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=18)** This is especially valuable knowledge because not every business can bake in the cost of shipping into their products.
>

> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-free-shipping?u=76281980&t=162)** Since you're using it as a tool to make more money, it's worth putting in a few places around your site.

#### Setting up live rates
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There are a few different ways to get live rates for your store.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=3)** For the most part, you'll have to install an extra plug-in to get live rates from shipping providers.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=9)** There's a ton of third party shipping services.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=11)** The most popular are USPS, UPS, and FedEx.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=16)** We're going to use the USPS extension, as it's one of the easier plug-ins to set up.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=20)** A lot of these plug-ins do require you to have an account, which means copying and pasting a bunch of API keys back and forth.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=26)** USPS has some default credentials you can use which will make setup much easier.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=31)** I'll go to my site, where I've already installed and activated the plug-in.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=35)** Then, we can go to WooCommerce, Settings, and now we can see USPS.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=39)** Let's click on that.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=42)** Here we can see the default API key, and if you ever have problems, you can enable Debug mode.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=48)** Going back to shipping zones, let's go to our local zone, and click Edit.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=55)** Let's scroll down and click Add Shipping Method.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=58)** Now we can see USPS as one of the options.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=61)** Let's go ahead and add that.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=66)** And now we can configure the settings.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=69)** Let's click Edit.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=72)** By default, this plug-in will only show you flat rate packages, which is useful for some merchants, but many merchants will have specific box sizes that they want to work with.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=81)** In that case, you will want to enable API Rates by checking this box.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=88)** Now you can adjust specific services and adjust the prices as you see fit.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=94)** These are all the API rates available to you.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=96)** We can adjust prices up or down, and we can disable certain services that we don't want.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=102)** For right now, let's leave all of these on, click Save Changes.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=107)** We'll go to our cart.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=110)** As you can see, now we see Priority Mail Flat Rate.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=114)** If you aren't getting any rates, you likely don't have USPS configured properly, or you haven't added a weight and dimensions to your products.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=121)** I know that I set a weight and dimensions right before this video, and I should be seeing a few more options right here.
>

>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=131)** I'll go back to my USPS settings, and it looks like I forgot the origin post code, so let's go ahead and set this.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=139)** We'll scroll back down, click Save Changes, refresh the cart, and now we can see all of the options available to us.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=149)** For right now, it's fine to show users a selection of services, but generally speaking, it's a bad idea to overwhelm people in the checkout.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-live-rates?u=76281980&t=156)** So if you don't see people using a particular service after a couple of months, then I recommend disabling it.

#### Printing shipping labels
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/printing-shipping-labels?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/printing-shipping-labels?u=76281980&t=0)** [Narrator] If you get a quote from USPS, or some other shipping provider, You still have to pack the boxes, bring them to the shipping office, get them weighed, measured.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/printing-shipping-labels?u=76281980&t=8)** And then, finally pay for them.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/printing-shipping-labels?u=76281980&t=10)** If you have ten orders going out, you could easily spend an hour or two doing all of that.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/printing-shipping-labels?u=76281980&t=14)** And you probably have something better that you can be doing with your time.
>

#### Consolidating multichannel shipping
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] As your business gets larger, or you start selling in mulitple marketplaces, you don't want to have to check multiple websites to see what packages you have to ship.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=8)** Instead, you may want to have a piece of software that aggregates all those orders into one place.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=14)** Going into detail in this process is a little bit out of scope of this course, but I want to provide you with some resources in case you think this may apply to you.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=22)** There are a ton of these services that integrate with WooCommerce and ShipStation is one of the more well-known services.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=28)** They automatically pull all of your orders into one interface which lets you mark items as shipped, print shipping labels, and get discount shipping prices.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=36)** And all this information travels back to WooCommerce so it's in both places.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=40)** Shippo is another well-known service which also has an integration with DHL which is a bit hard to find.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=46)** So if you need DHL, I'd look into this service.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=49)** Another popular option is ShippingEasy, which again, is really good at aggregating all these orders.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=54)** As a business owner, it's much easier to give someone access to your shipping software than to give them the keys to your website.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/consolidating-multichannel-shipping?u=76281980&t=60)** So as soon as you get big enough to have a helper, having a service like this just for shipping can be insanely useful.

### 6. Setting Up Payment

#### Configuring payment options
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] To have a true ecommerce site, you need to be able to accept payment online.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=4)** Being able to take payment turns your website from a catalog into a real store.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=8)** There's a couple of ways that this can happen.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=10)** Someone can log into an account where they keep their virtual money, and they could transfer it to your account.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=15)** A good example of this would be PayPal, which we'll set up in a future video.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=18)** Another option is for someone to type in their credit card details into your site and use technology on your side to communicate with a bank to validate and draw funds.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=27)** An example of this would be Stripe, which we'll also set up in a future video.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=33)** Now, all of this might sound a bit complicated, and that's because it is complicated.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=37)** With credit cards, there's two important steps.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=40)** The first is they have to verify the funds.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=43)** Next, they have to draw and deposit the funds.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=47)** We don't need to go into the details right now.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=49)** What you need to know is that modern payment gateways like Stripe will take care of all of this.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=53)** They verify the funds, draw them, and they deposit those funds into your business bank account.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=58)** All you need to do is make sure your site is secure.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=61)** You need an SSL certificate when you take the credit card payments on your own site.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=65)** When an SSL certificate is set up correctly, you can see the little lock icon in the address bar of your browser, and that means that all the information you send back and forth to the website is encrypted and protected.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=75)** Setting up an SSL certificate used to be very complicated, but because of Let's Encrypt, you can now get free SSL certificates.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=81)** If you're using a good host, they'll have a button in your hosting account to get a free SSL certificate for your site, or they'll automatically create your site with an SSL certificate.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=91)** If you can't get an SSL certificate, you'll want to find a new host since you will need this for ecommerce.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=97)** Once you have an SSL certificate installed on your site, you can force the entire site to load over HTTPS since it's better security all around, so try that option first.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=107)** To do that, in WordPress we can go to our general settings and then change the WordPress address right here to make sure it loads over HTTPS.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=115)** Some payment gateways will show you warnings until you force your site to load over HTTPS this way.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-payment-options?u=76281980&t=120)** So if you're seeing some warnings about not loading over HTTPS, make sure to change it here.
