#### Setting up PayPal
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of the most popular payment solutions is PayPal, and that's for a couple of reasons.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=5)** The first is that it's incredibly easy to set up, both for the merchants and for the customers.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=10)** The PayPal gateway built into WooCommerce only requires an email address.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=14)** That's the easiest setup for any gateway.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=16)** The other reason is that many people keep their spending money in their PayPal accounts.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=20)** There's a greater chance for someone to spend that money than the money in their bank accounts.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=25)** Another reason is that people feel safe using PayPal, both because PayPal is very safe and because people have a small amount of money in their accounts to start with.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=33)** If there was a security issue, they'd lose a relatively small amount of money, compared to someone getting ahold of their credit card and spending thousands.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=41)** For all of these reasons, people love PayPal.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=43)** Some online stores get over 50% of their revenue from PayPal.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=47)** At the very least, it's worth setting up PayPal just to see how important it is for your business.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=52)** If you have a product or audience that doesn't cater to people with PayPal accounts, you can always remove that option down the road.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=58)** So let's go ahead and configure PayPal.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=60)** We'll go to our WooCommerce site.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=63)** Let's go to WooCommerce, Settings, Payments.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=70)** And if we scroll down, we can see PayPal.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=74)** Let's go ahead and turn that on.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=76)** And if you enabled PayPal through the welcome wizard, you'll also see WooCommerce PayPal Checkout Payment Gateway in the list of options.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=84)** If you don't see it, make sure you install and active this free plugin.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=88)** There are tons of different versions of PayPal available to WooCommerce stores.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=91)** I recommend that stores first experiment with PayPal Standard, which is built into WooCommerce, and see if their audience even uses PayPal.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=99)** If so and you like that option, then go ahead and get the WooCommerce PayPal Checkout Payment Gateway plugin.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=104)** It gives you a little bit more configuration.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=106)** However, you need a business account, which takes a little bit more setup from within PayPal.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=111)** I mostly want my customers to use Stripe for credit cards, so I'm keeping PayPal as a backup option.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=115)** So I'm going to set up the simpler PayPal Standard method.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=119)** We're going to configure this PayPal.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=121)** Let's click Set up.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=124)** The first two fields are about turning on PayPal and possibly turning it on for subscriptions if you have that installed.

>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=134)** These are both used to describe the payment method to the customers as they're checking out.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=138)** Most people are familiar with PayPal, so I don't think I need to add anything here.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=142)** The PayPal email field is the email address associated with your PayPal account.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=146)** Further down the page is PayPal sandbox, which is a test environment.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=151)** If you turn this on, it means you can make test transactions with a test purchasing account and receive that money in another test PayPal account.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=157)** It's a bit putzy to keep track of all of your test accounts, but it is definitely worth doing to make sure that payment is working correctly.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=164)** You can make a few test purchases before you make your store live.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=167)** The debug log automatically logs a few pieces of information during the payment process.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=172)** If you ever have problems with payment, look into this log to see where payment stopped.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=176)** You might see an error in there which can be Googled to figure out the issue.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=179)** You can keep this on right now since the site isn't live, but I recommend turning it off once you've made a few test transactions.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=185)** You shouldn't log everything.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=186)** Only log when you think you might have a problem.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=189)** Further on down, there are some more advanced options, and there's two that I want to point out.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=193)** The first is the PayPal identity token.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=197)** Some websites have issues with something called the PayPal IPN.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=200)** That is the instant payment notification sent from PayPal to your site.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=205)** Without that, your site doesn't know that the order was actually paid for and will leave the order as unpaid in WooCommerce, which is not good.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=212)** To get around that, you can configure Payment Data Transfer, or PDT, in PayPal, and that will circumvent the IPN.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=220)** So if you have unpaid orders in WooCommerce, but they're marked as paid in PayPal, definitely look into this setting.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=225)** Or consider setting up WooCommerce PayPal Checkout Payment Gateway which we mentioned earlier, since it doesn't use this system.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=231)** The other setting that might be worth implementing is the PayPal API.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=235)** Later in this course when we look at managing orders, one of the things you can do is refund directly in WooCommerce.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=241)** With the API enabled, you can mark an order as refunded in WooCommerce, and the order will automatically be refunded through PayPal.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=248)** That's a huge time-saver and prevents inconsistent data and confusion.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=252)** You don't need to do this to launch your store, so I recommend doing it the first time you get a refund request.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=257)** Spend a couple extra minutes following the link here to set up the API so all future refund requests will go much faster.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-paypal?u=76281980&t=263)** When you're done with your PayPal settings, just click Save changes, and now you can accept PayPal payments the way you want.

> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=234)** And lastly there is saved cards.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=236)** Saving credit card information is a huge time saver for the user, and it prevents all sorts of silly mistakes, like typing in the credit card number incorrectly.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=244)** But the one important thing to note is that your site isn't storing the credit card number, it's storing something called a token.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=249)** A token is a representation of a credit card number.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=253)** Think of it as a special password just for your site.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=255)** So if your site tells Stripe the password for a particular customer, Stripe will use the credit card number.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=261)** Stripe is the one that's actually saving the information here.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=264)** If someone ever happened to steal that special password and they gave it to Stripe, Stripe wouldn't process the card because it's specific to your account.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=271)** In that way, tokens are much safer.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=274)** If someone hacked your site, it's very unlikely that they'd be able to do anything with those tokens, so they're very safe.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=280)** That's why I recommend enabling payment via saved cards.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=283)** And the last setting here is logging.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=285)** You can turn this on if you're having problems with Stripe.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=287)** Make a couple test transactions and go onto the log and see exactly what's happening.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=291)** I added this functionality to Stripe myself just to make sure that I can track down any weird bugs.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=296)** There are almost never any bugs, but it's nice to have a log, just in case.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=300)** When you launch, make sure to turn off Test Mode and make sure you have a live Stripe account ready to go with live keys.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=307)** Save your settings and you're ready to accept credit card payments.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/setting-up-stripe?u=76281980&t=308)** to accept credit card payments.

#### Configuring additional payment methods
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] You may have noticed there's a lot more than just PayPal and Stripe.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=4)** Just in the core WooCommerce plugin, there are three more options: Direct bank transfer, check payments, and cash on delivery.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=10)** Now these are what I consider offline payments, since there's no immediate way to accept payment.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=15)** For the most part, you can go in here and turn on or off the method and it'll be available in checkout.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=21)** If a user checks out with this method, their order will go on hold and as soon as you have confirmation of payment, you can change the status of this order to processing or completed.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=30)** But in addition to these offline methods, there are additional online methods, for example, Amazon Pay.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=37)** At checkout, there's a button that lets a user check out with their Amazon accounts.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=41)** It's super secure and really easy to set up.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=43)** If you think your customers are also Amazon customers, then it might be worth adding this button, as it's similar to PayPal where users just have to have an account already set up.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=52)** If you already have a brick and mortar store, as well as an online store, you might want to consider using Square.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=58)** That way, you have one payment processor for all of your transactions.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=62)** It's going to be less paperwork on your end, and the Square extension from WooCommerce can also sink your inventory between your online store and your physical store.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=73)** We've covered only a few of the many hundred payment gateways, and all of them are slightly different.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=78)** If you're brand new to e-commerce, I strongly recommend Stripe and PayPal, but if for some reason you can't use those, then you could find dozens more on [WooCommerce.com](https://WooCommerce.com).
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=87)** You may have noticed over the past couple videos a banner about PayPal Standard and WooCommerce Subscriptions.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=92)** If you have both WooCommerce Subscriptions activated and you've configured PayPal Standard, you'll see this banner on the Plugins page and a few other pages.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=100)** I don't want to clutter up the admin for the rest of this course.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=103)** So for the sake of demonstration, I'm going to deactivate WooCommerce Subscriptions.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-additional-payment-methods?u=76281980&t=107)** If you want to use subscriptions with PayPal, then you could follow the instructions to set up the API which will hide this banner.

### 7. Setting Up Taxes

#### Configuring tax settings
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=0)** - If you run an Ecommerce store, you'll have to know how to charge taxes during checkout.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=5)** But before we get into actually adding tax rates, we should configure the basic tax settings.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=9)** In the Admin of your site, you can go to WooCommerce, settings, and then tax.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=15)** If you're using automated taxes which we setup in the Welcome Wizard, you shouldn't have to do anything.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=20)** In fact, most of the screen will be grayed out so you can't mess it up.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=23)** If you're using automated taxes, you're done and you can skip to the next chapter.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=28)** But if you aren't using automated taxes because you have a more complicated tax setup with nexus and multiple tax jurisdictions, then you'll want to know how to manually configure all of these tax settings.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=38)** So what I'm going to do here is temporarily disable automated taxes.

>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=47)** There are a lot of options on this screen.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=49)** If you want to know why this screen is so complicated it's so that WooCommerce can be configured to work in just about any country.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=56)** Most of this you won't need.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=57)** But there are a few settings that we should touch on.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=60)** The first is how you want to display your taxes.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=63)** Displaying prices excluding tax is common in United States.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=67)** So you display the product price at $9.99 on the product page and the tax gets added during the checkout and may make it more expensive.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=74)** Tax inclusive prices are common in Europe.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=78)** They show the price of the product with taxes included so nothing gets added at checkout.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=82)** If you see a product for $10 you pay $10 at checkout.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=85)** Unless you have a very unique situation, I recommend setting all of your inclusive, exclusive settings to the same value.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=92)** So exclusive here and exclusive here and here.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=95)** The calculate tax based on setting will likely be set to shipping address.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=99)** There are a couple of options here.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=101)** Usually, you calculate taxes based on where the person is buying from.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=105)** Either their shipping address or their billing address.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=108)** If you go with the bottom option, you basically use your local tax rate for every single transaction.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=112)** Check with your tax professional if you think you need this setting.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=115)** Another setting you might want to look at is display tax totals at the bottom of the screen.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=120)** I've seen this in different formats in physical brick and mortar stores and online stores.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=125)** Basically, if you have multiple overlapping taxes WooCommerce is asking you if you want to merge them together or if you want to list them separately.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=133)** So you might have a state tax and then if you're in a special zip code there's sometimes extra taxes.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=137)** For example, if you're in a city that has a public sports team, there might be a stadium tax.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=142)** You could list these separately on the checkout page.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=145)** Generally speaking, users don't need to know exactly where every cent of tax is going.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=149)** I recommend merging all of your taxes together.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=152)** Automated taxes can really help you set some of these defaults.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=155)** But whether you choose to use automated taxes or you manually set these settings you should always double check these with a tax professional.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/configuring-tax-settings?u=76281980&t=162)** And then click save changes to make sure everything is saved.

#### Using additional tax rates
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We set up our standard rates which is great for most stores, but some goods require extra tax rules.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=6)** For example in the U.S., depending on which area you're in some types of food, clothing, or medicine will have either a reduced tax rate or be tax exempt.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=15)** To set these up, go to the Admin and under WooCommerce, Settings, Tax, you can see reduced rate rates and zero rate rates.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=23)** Let's say the supplement we sell has a reduced rate.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=25)** I'm going to go ahead and add a reduced rate and then apply it to that supplement product.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=31)** So let's go to reduced rate and before I go I'm just going to remember that the Colorado tax is 8.31.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=39)** So I'll add a new row here, I'll add all the information I had before and instead of 8.31 I'll put in 4.31.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=51)** I'll go ahead and save these changes and now we have a tax setting saved, but WooCommerce doesn't know which products use the reduced rate rate and which products use the standard rate rate.

> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=72)** Click Update.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=75)** And now WooCommerce knows that this product uses a special tax class and is calculated separately.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=80)** Go ahead and do this with all of your reduced rate and zero rate products.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/using-additional-tax-rates?u=76281980&t=84)** Just make sure to check with a tax professional before you launch your store.

#### Connecting your store to TaxJar
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So far everything we've done has been manual and requires a bit of effort on your part.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=5)** If you want to save yourself a bit of work setting all this up, there's a number of services that can automate your tax collection and even help you file taxes at the end of the year.

>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=20)** The lowest plan is $17 a month.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=22)** And for the amount of time it save you at the end of the year, this could be very cost effective.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=26)** If you aren't using automated taxes, and you want to save yourself some time, Tax Jar is one of the best options out there.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=33)** You can sign up and install their free plugin and automate most of the work with your taxes.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=38)** And they also offer some of those premium services, like helping you file your sales tax in multiple states.

> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=43)** And just in case you want to see how much they know about taxes, I encourage you to look at one of their state guides for sales tax.

> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/connecting-your-store-to-taxjar?u=76281980&t=50)** They are very thorough and these people know a lot about taxes.

### 8. Connecting to Services

#### Installing Google Analytics
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There's a lot of things that you should do after you launch your store.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=3)** But one of the few things I recommend every store owner do, either before launch, or immediately after launch, is to setup Google analytics.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=10)** And that's because the service is so useful to understand where people are coming from and what they're doing on your store before they buy.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=17)** It's also a free service, so it won't take any of your limited funds.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=21)** You can set it up early, and just let it collect data for a while.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=25)** Even if you don't use it for a year when you do eventually decide to use it you'll have a ton of useful data.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=30)** What you don't want is to get stuck in a place where you need the data and it's not setup.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=34)** And you have to wait a month to get solid data.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=36)** And in that month your business gets into trouble.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=39)** There's a free plugin built by the WooCommerce team that will send all of your traffic and eCommerce data to Google analytics.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=45)** This plugin will handle all of your needs and you don't have to have another Google analytics integration.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=50)** Now, if you're already using a different plugin for Google analytics such as MonsterInsights, then you'll either have to switch analytics plugins or you can get their eCommerce add on.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/installing-google-analytics?u=76281980&t=61)** I'm going to show you the free WooCommerce Google analytics integration.

>

#### Managing refunds
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Managing orders, printing shipping labels, and marking orders as complete is pretty straightforward, but sometimes you'll have a customer who wants a refund.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=8)** And depending on the payment gateways you've set up, this can either be a snap or a pretty big pain.

>

>

>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=43)** We can press Tab a few times and WooCommerce automatically calculates that we're going to refund them $54.16, and we can say, customer only wanted one.

>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=61)** So hopefully, in the near future, WooCommerce has made this a little bit more intuitive, because sometimes you just want to type the refund amount right here and not fiddle with the exact quantity up here.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=71)** It's worth pointing out that WooCommerce doesn't automatically recalculate shipping costs or discounts from coupons.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=78)** Technically, with just five products, we drop below the free shipping threshold and we can ask the customer to pay for shipping or deduct the cost of shipping from their refund, but I think most store owners are pretty generous with refunds, so probably just refund them and not worry about technically being ineligible for that free shipping.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=97)** Either way, once you've selected the items you want to refund, you can either manually or automatically refund the payment.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=103)** If your gateway supports automatic refunds, you will want to click this button.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=107)** This saves you a ton of busywork.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=109)** Some older gateways don't support this and you'll have to refund in WooCommerce, log into your gateway, find the transaction and manually refund the payment.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=116)** That is what this means.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=118)** Since we use Stripe, it's just a simple as a button.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=122)** Once you refund something, you'll see a new updated total and the refund is logged underneath the existing items.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=128)** The order will also be marked as refunded if all of the items, including shipping and tax, are refunded.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=135)** One thing I want to mention is I recommended PayPal Standard earlier in this course.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=139)** I do really like this option, but if you do a lot of refunds, you have to do a lot of extra work.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-refunds?u=76281980&t=145)** So if you start getting refunds, you'll either want to configure the API option in PayPal Standard or you'll want to switch to this gateway which we also recommended, which is available for free and has much better refund support.

> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-reports?u=76281980&t=75)** So, always compare it to the previous year or the previous period.

> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/managing-reports?u=76281980&t=80)** For example: this month compared to last month.

>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=60)** The next setting down here is just related to shipping.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=63)** So you might want to allow digital sales globally but not have to worry about international shipping.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=67)** In which case you can just disable a couple of really far away countries.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=71)** The default customer location is used when someone visits your site and they haven't logged in.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=75)** They haven't gone to the cart or checkout yet, so your site has no idea where they're from.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=80)** The default is to take a guess with geolocation.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=83)** You're basically using their IP address, and checking it against a list of known IP addresses to guess where they're located.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=88)** The reason you might want to do this is because certain countries have laws about how prices have to appear online.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=94)** So if you're in the European Union, there are laws about including tax of the product in the price you see online.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=99)** So if you're a US company and you have nexus in the EU, you might want to show customers prices with that included.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=106)** To do that, you have to take a guess where they're from, and geolocation is one of the best ways to do that.
>

>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=120)** Sometimes they aggressively cache pages, and they're unfortunately shared between different customers.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=125)** If you select this option, you append a query string to a page, which looks something like question mark, A equals one, two, three, four, five, six seven, eight, nine, which will force your site to load a whole new page.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=134)** It makes the URL slightly less pretty, but it works very well against aggressively caching systems.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/general-settings?u=76281980&t=139)** I recommend leaving this to the default until you notice a problem.

>

>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=102)** When someone places an order on your site and then they go to PayPal to pay for their order, some users forget their passwords, they don't have enough money in their account, or for whatever reason, they don't actually pay for their order.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=113)** WooCommerce sets the order to pending and waits until the allotted time is up.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=117)** That's this number right here.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=119)** If it expires, the stock is available again for someone else to purchase.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=123)** So WooCommerce uses this number as a sort of reservation system for offsite gateways.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=128)** You can set this to whatever number you want.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=130)** If you're using a gateway like Stripe that does it instantly, you don't even need to worry about this.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=134)** If I use PayPal, I tend to set it to 1,440, which is exactly one day.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=141)** If the user doesn't pay within a day, the order is canceled, and the stock is returned.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=146)** These next settings are about notifications.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=148)** WooCommerce will notify you when your stock gets below a certain point.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=152)** This is super useful.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=153)** If you know that you tend to sell 10 units a week, and it takes a week to get new units, you probably want to set the Low Stock Notification to 10.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=160)** If you have a bit more capital, you could set it to 15 or 20, just to make sure you never run out of stock.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=166)** Out of stock is still helpful, and of course, you want to make sure you send it to the right person.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=170)** The next setting lets you hide out-of-stock products.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=173)** I don't normally recommend this.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=174)** It's only useful if you have so many out-of-stock products that users can't find products in stock.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=179)** Generally, it's best to leave your product page up when it's out of stock.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=183)** People will find it, and they might even write you and ask when it's back in stock.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=187)** There's even a few premium plug ins that will let users go on a wait list and will automatically be emailed when the product comes back into stock.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=195)** This is much preferable to hiding the item altogether.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=198)** The next setting is about showing this remaining stock.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=201)** I like to change this to Only show quantity remaining when the stock is low.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=206)** I'll click Save Changes.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=208)** And the last tab is for downloadable products.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=211)** There are three different ways to serve these downloaded files.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=214)** Force downloads is good, but won't work with every server.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=217)** If you have problems, then I recommend Redirect only.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=221)** If you want, you can see a bit more about the nuances between these methods.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=225)** I recommend leaving the other settings as they are.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=228)** The next option would force users to log in, which isn't great.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=231)** And the last option makes the user wait until you change an order status from Processing to Completed before they download their files.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=237)** Once they've paid, they should have access, so I'll leave these as they are.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/product-settings?u=76281980&t=240)** And that'll take care of the product settings.

#### Email settings
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before we get into e-mail settings themselves, I want to touch on e-mail deliverability.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=5)** At WooCommerce store, we'll send a lot of e-mails.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=8)** They're multiple e-mails sent to the customer, low stock notifications, e-mails sent to the store owner, etc.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=14)** And webservers aren't typically set up in such a way to be able to send that many e-mails and sometimes those e-mails fail.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=21)** Not getting an e-mail about a new order could be a pretty big problem.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=25)** You don't log in because you don't think there's an order, and your customer just sits there and gets more and more frustrated until they initiate a charge back which costs you money.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=34)** There is a solution to this problem.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=36)** You can set up a free account with a SMTP provider.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=39)** Basically, a company that will send out all of your e-mail for you, with servers that are built so that e-mails won't fail.

>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=54)** We won't go through account creation here, but it's worth setting up a free account to make sure all of your e-mails go through successfully.

>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=68)** Now let's go back to our e-mail settings.

> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/email-settings?u=76281980&t=100)** We won't go into customizing e-mails in this course, but it's covered in detail in my WordPress, Customizing WooCommerce Themes course, here in the library.

#### Integrating with 3rd party platforms
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you look at your Settings screen right now you might not see an Integration tab, and that's because it only shows up when you have an active integration.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=8)** Because we have a few integrations active, I can see this tab, and there will be sub-tabs for each individual integration.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=15)** Most integrations with third party services will show up here, so if you plan to connect to other services, look for their settings right here.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=22)** However, some services use the WooCommerce API to connect.

> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=26)** We can find the API under Advanced, and then Rest API.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=33)** This page lets you create a key that another application can use to get all of the data from your store.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=39)** Let's create one just to show you how to do it.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=41)** So if I really want to connect my store to a custom warehouse pick and packing app on my phone so I can see what's happening at all times, I'll create a new API key, and I'll call this the Test API key, and I can assign it to myself, that's fine, and then Permissions.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=58)** Read means it can access all the data on my store, but it can't make any changes.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=63)** Write means it can send data, but it can't read anything, and then Read and Write means you can do both, access and update data.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=70)** As a rule of thumb, don't give people more access than they need.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=73)** If you're connecting to an analytics service, just give them access to read your site.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=77)** If you're connecting to some sort of shipping app that reads orders and then can also update the status of those orders, you'll likely have to give them both read and write access.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=85)** Go ahead and generate the API key, and here's all the information we need to connect to the store.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=93)** One note, if you leave this page and try to come back, you won't be able to see the full key, and you'll have to create a new one.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=101)** There is one more thing to cover, and those are webhooks.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=104)** Think of webhooks as a way to automatically send data to a service without needing an API.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=109)** So you could automatically send a service information about each new order with a webhook.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=114)** This can be useful, but they're a bit of a pain to set up and I generally recommend setting up and installing plug-ins for services before trying to use webhooks that can be set up incorrectly.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=123)** If some service requires webhooks, they'll tell you how to configure them.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=127)** Just know that there's a page for them right here.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=129)** There's one sub-tab under Advanced that we didn't look at yet, and that is Page Setup.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=135)** Here we can see the Cart, Checkout, My Account, and Terms and Conditions page, and by default, Terms and Conditions should be empty.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=144)** If you ever wanted to use a different page for cart or checkout for some reason, you could do so.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=148)** Just change it to whatever page you want.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=150)** For your terms and conditions, you'll want to find a generator online, copy and paste it into its own page, and then select that page here.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=157)** These terms and conditions will show up automatically during the checkout, and users will have to agree to them.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=163)** Let's go ahead and do that quickly.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=164)** I'll just select a random page here, I'll click About, save these changes, and let's go to the front end.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=179)** Proceed to Checkout.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=183)** And here you can see I have read and agreed to the website's terms and conditions, which links to the page we selected just a minute ago.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=190)** Let's go back to our settings.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=192)** The next group are what are called end points.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=195)** Think of them as WordPress pages without actually being pages.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=198)** They look and feel like a page, but you can't edit the content.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=202)** The content is all dynamic based on who logs in and it comes from WooCommerce.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=206)** So you could change the URL.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=209)** And the last thing that's worth mentioning, some plug-ins, like WooCommerce Subscriptions have so many settings that they'll create their own Settings tab, either up here, or they'll add settings to one of these tabs.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/wordpress-ecommerce-woocommerce-4/integrating-with-3rd-party-platforms?u=76281980&t=219)** So if you have some complicated WooCommerce extensions, look for the settings up here.
